struct {\n    69→\t// nodeToStatus contains specific statuses of the nodes.\n    70→\tnodeToStatus map[string]*Status\n    71→\t// absentNodesStatus defines a status for all nodes that are absent in nodeToStatus map.\n    72→\t// By default, all absent nodes are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n    73→\tabsentNodesStatus *Status\n    74→}\n    75→\n    76→// NewDefaultNodeToStatus creates NodeToStatus without any node in the map.\n    77→// The absentNodesStatus is set by default to UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n    78→func NewDefaultNodeToStatus() *NodeToStatus {\n    79→\treturn NewNodeToStatus(make(map[string]*Status), NewStatus(UnschedulableAndUnresolvable))\n    80→}\n    81→\n    82→// NewNodeToStatus creates NodeToStatus initialized with given nodeToStatus and set.\n   119→// Imporatant note, it runs the fn only for nodes with a status explicitly registered,\n   120→// and hence may not run the fn for all existing nodes.\n   121→// For example, if PreFilter rejects all Nodes, the scheduler would NOT set a failure status to every Node,\n   122→// but set a failure status as AbsentNodesStatus.\n   123→// You're supposed to get a status from AbsentNodesStatus(), and consider all other nodes that are rejected by them.\n   124→func (m *NodeToStatus) ForEachExplicitNode(fn func(nodeName string, status *Status)) {\n   125→\tfor nodeName, status := range m.nodeToStatus {\n   126→\t\tfn(nodeName, status)\n   127→\t}\n   128→}\n   129→\n   130→// NodesForStatusCode returns a list of NodeInfos for the nodes that matches a given status code.\n   131→// If the absentNodesStatus matches the code, all existing nodes are fetched using nodeLister\n   132→// and filtered using NodeToStatus.Get.\n   133→// If the absentNodesStatus doesn't match the code, nodeToStatus map is used to create a list of nodes\n   134→// and nodeLister.Get is used to obtain NodeInfo for each.\n   135→func (m *NodeToStatus) NodesForStatusCode(nodeLister NodeInfoLister, code Code) ([]*NodeInfo, error) {\n   136→\tvar resultNodes []*NodeInfo\n   137→\n   138→\tif m.AbsentNodesStatus().Code() == code {\n   139→\t\tallNodes, err := nodeLister.List()\n   140→\t\tif err != nil {\n   141→\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   142→\t\t}\n   143→\t\tif m.Len() == 0 {\n   144→\t\t\t// All nodes are absent and status code is matching, so can return all nodes.\n   145→\t\t\treturn allNodes, nil\n   146→\t\t}\n   147→\t\t// Need to find all the nodes that are absent or have a matching code using the allNodes.\n   148→\t\tfor _, node := range allNodes {\n   149→\t\t\tnodeName := node.Node().Name\n   150→\t\t\tif status := m.Get(nodeName); status.Code() == code {\n   151→\t\t\t\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, node)\n   152→\t\t\t}\n   153→\t\t}\n   154→\t\treturn resultNodes, nil\n   155→\t}\n   156→\n   157→\tm.ForEachExplicitNode(func(nodeName string, status *Status) {\n   158→\t\tif status.Code() == code {\n   159→\t\t\tif nodeInfo, err := nodeLister.Get(nodeName); err == nil {\n   160→\t\t\t\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, nodeInfo)\n   161→\t\t\t}\n   162→\t\t}\n   163→\t})\n   164→\n   165→\treturn resultNodes, nil\n   166→}\n   167→\n   168→// NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\n   169→type NodePluginScores struct {\n   170→\t// Name is node name.\n   171→\tName string\n   172→\t// Scores 185→// Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\n   186→type Code int\n   187→\n   188→// These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n   189→// Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\n   190→const (\n   191→\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n   192→\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n   193→\tSuccess Code = iota\n   194→\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n   195→\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n   196→\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n   197→\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n   198→\tError\n   199→\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n   200→\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n   201→\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n   202→\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n   203→\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n   204→\t//\n   205→\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n   206→\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n   207→\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n   208→\tUnschedulable\n   209→\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n   210→\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n   211→\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n   212→\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n   213→\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n   214→\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n   215→\t//\n   216→\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n   217→\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n   218→\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n   219→\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n   220→\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n   221→\tWait\n   222→\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n   223→\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n   224→\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n   225→\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n   226→\tSkip\n   227→\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n   228→\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n   229→\t//\n   230→\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n   231→\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n   232→\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n   233→\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n   234→\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n   235→\t//\n   236→\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n   237→\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n   238→\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n   239→\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n   240→\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n   241→\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n   242→\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n   243→\tPending\n   244→)\n   245→\n   246→// This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\n   247→var codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n   248→\n   249→func (c Code) String() string {\n   250→\treturn codes[c]\n   251→}\n   252→\n   253→const (\n   254→\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score 259→\n   260→\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n   261→\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n   262→)\n   263→\n   264→// PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n   265→// If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n   266→// activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n   267→// - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n   289→// message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n   290→// When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n   291→// And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n   292→// NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\n   293→type Status struct {\n   294→\tcode    Code\n   295→\treasons []string\n   296→\terr     error\n   297→\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n   298→\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n   299→\tplugin string\n   300→}\n   301→\n   302→func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n   303→\ts.err = err\n   304→\treturn s\n   305→}\n   306→\n   307→// Code returns code of the Status.\n   308→func (s *Status) Code() Code {\n   309→\tif s == nil {\n   310→\t\treturn Success\n   311→\t}\n   312→\treturn s.code\n   313→}\n   314→\n   315→// Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n   316→func (s *Status) Message() string {\n   317→\tif s == nil {\n   318→\t\treturn \"\"\n   319→\t}\n   320→\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n   321→}\n   322→\n   323→// SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\n   324→func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n   325→\ts.plugin = plugin\n   326→}\n   327→\n   328→// WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n   329→// and returns the given status object.\n   330→func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n   331→\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n   332→\treturn s\n   333→}\n   334→\n   335→// Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\n   336→func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n   337→\treturn s.plugin\n   338→}\n   339→\n   340→// Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\n   341→func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n   342→\tif s.err != nil {\n   343→\t\treturn AppendReason(reason string) {\n   350→\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n   351→}\n   352→\n   353→// IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\n   354→func IsSkip() bool {\n   365→\treturn s.Code() == Skip\n   366→}\n   367→\n   368→// IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\n   369→func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n   370→\tcode := s.Code()\n   371→\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n   372→}\n   373→\n   374→// AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n   375→// with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n   376→func (s *Status) AsError() error {\n   377→\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n   378→\t\treturn nil\n   379→\t}\n   380→\tif s.err != nil {\n   381→\t\treturn s.err\n   382→\t}\n   383→\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n   384→}\n   385→\n   386→// Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n   387→// cmp.Equal.\n   388→func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n   389→\tif s == nil || x == nil {\n   390→\t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n   391→\t}\n   392→\tif s.code != x.code {\n   393→\t\treturn false\n   394→\t}\n   395→\tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n   396→\t\treturn false\n   397→\t}\n   398→\tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n   399→\t\treturn false\n   400→\t}\n   401→\treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n   402→}\n   403→\n   404→func (s *Status) String() string {\n   405→\treturn s.Message()\n   406→}\n   407→\n   408→// NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\n   409→func NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n   410→\ts := interface {\n   444→\tName() string\n   445→}\n   446→\n   447→// PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n   448→// These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n   449→// Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n   450→// involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n   451→// Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\n   452→type PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n   453→\tPlugin\n   454→\t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n   455→\tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n   456→}\n   457→\n   458→// LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\n   459→type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n   460→\n   461→// QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n   462→// These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n   463→// plugin may be enabled at a time.\n   464→type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n   465→\tPlugin\n   466→\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n   467→\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n   468→}\n   469→\n   470→// EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n   471→// move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n   472→// In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n   473→// and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n   474→// Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n   475→// and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n   476→// This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n   477→// and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n   478→//\n   479→// Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n   480→// otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n   481→// And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n   482→type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n   483→\tPlugin\n   484→\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n   485→\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n   486→\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n   487→\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n   488→\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n   489→\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\n   490→\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\n   491→\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\n   492→\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\n   493→\t//\n   494→\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n   495→\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\n   496→}\n   497→\n   498→// PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n   499→// callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n   500→// state.\n   501→type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n   502→\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n   503→\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n   504→\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n   505→\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n   506→\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n   507→\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n   508→}\n   509→\n   510→// PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n   511→// These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\n   512→type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n   513→\tPlugin\n   514→\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n   515→\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n   516→\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n   517→\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n   518→\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n   519→\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n   520→\t//\n   521→\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n   522→\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n   523→\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n   524→\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n   525→\t// or nil if it does not. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n   527→\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n   528→\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n   529→\t// Filter again on a specific node.\n   530→\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n   531→}\n   532→\n   533→// FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n   534→// filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n   535→// This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n   536→// These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n   537→// However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n   538→// Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n   539→// running the pod.\n   540→type FilterPlugin interface {\n   541→\tPlugin\n   542→\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n   543→\t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n   544→\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n   545→\t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n   546→\t//\n   547→\t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n   548→\t//\n   549→\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n   550→\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n   551→\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n   552→\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n   553→\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n   554→\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n   555→\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n   556→\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n   557→}\n   558→\n   559→// PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n   560→// after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n   561→type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n   562→\tPlugin\n   563→\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n   564→\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n   565→\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n   566→\t//\n   567→\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n   568→\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n   569→\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n   570→\t//\n   571→\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n   572→\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n   573→\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n   574→\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n   575→\t//\n   576→\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n   577→\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. NodeToStatus contains the statuses of the Nodes where the incoming Pod was not schedulable.\ntype NodeToStatus struct {\n\t// nodeToStatus contains specific statuses of the nodes.\n\tnodeToStatus nodeToStatus,\n\t\tabsentNodesStatus: absentNodesStatus,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Get returns the status for given nodeName. If the node is not in the map, the absentNodesStatus is returned.\nfunc (m *NodeToStatus) Get(nodeName string) *Status {\n\tif status, ok := m.nodeToStatus[nodeName]; ok {\n\t\treturn status\n\t}\n\treturn m.absentNodesStatus\n}\n\n// Set sets status for given nodeName.\nfunc (m *NodeToStatus) Set(nodeName string, status *Status) {\n\tm.nodeToStatus[nodeName] = status\n}\n\n// Len returns length of nodeToStatus map. {\n\tm.absentNodesStatus = status\n}\n\n// ForEachExplicitNode runs fn for each node which status is explicitly set.\n// Imporatant note, it runs the fn only for nodes with a status explicitly registered,\n// and hence may not run the fn for all existing nodes.\n// For example, if PreFilter rejects all Nodes, the scheduler would NOT set a failure status to every Node,\n// but set a failure status as AbsentNodesStatus.\n// You're supposed to get a status from AbsentNodesStatus(), and consider all other nodes that are rejected by them.\nfunc (m *NodeToStatus) ForEachExplicitNode(fn func(nodeName string, status *Status)) {\n\tfor nodeName, status := range m.nodeToStatus {\n\t\tfn(nodeName, status)\n\t}\n}\n\n// NodesForStatusCode returns a list of NodeInfos for the nodes that matches a given status code.\n// If the absentNodesStatus matches the code, all existing nodes are fetched using nodeLister\n// and filtered using NodeToStatus.Get.\n// If the absentNodesStatus doesn't match the code, nodeToStatus map is used to create a list of nodes\n// and nodeLister.Get is used to obtain NodeInfo for each.\nfunc (m *NodeToStatus) NodesForStatusCode(nodeLister NodeInfoLister, code Code) ([]*NodeInfo, error) {\n\tvar resultNodes []*NodeInfo\n\n\tif m.AbsentNodesStatus().Code() == code {\n\t\tallNodes, err := nodeLister.List()\n\t\tif err != nil the nodes that are absent or have a matching code using the allNodes.\n\t\tfor _, node := range allNodes {\n\t\t\tnodeName := node.Node().Name\n\t\t\tif status := m.Get(nodeName); status.Code() == code {\n\t\t\t\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, node)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn resultNodes, nil\n\t}\n\n\tm.ForEachExplicitNode(func(nodeName string, status *Status) {\n\t\tif status.Code() == code {\n\t\t\tif nodeInfo, err := nodeLister.Get(nodeName); err == nil {\n\t\t\t\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, nodeInfo)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t})\n\n\treturn resultNodes, nil\n}\n\n// NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\ntype NodePluginScores struct {\n\t// Name is node name.\n\tName string\n\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\n\tScores []PluginScore\n\t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\n\tTotalScore int64\n}\n\n// PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\ntype PluginScore struct {\n\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\n\tName  string\n\tScore int64\n}\n\n// Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\ntype Code int\n\n// These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n// Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\nconst (\n\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n\tSuccess Code = iota\n\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n\tError\n\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulable\n\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n\tWait\n\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n\tSkip\n\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n\t//\n\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n\tPending\n)\n\n// This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\nvar codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n\nfunc (c Code) String() string {\n\treturn codes[c]\n}\n\nconst (\n\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\n\n\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\n\n\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n)\n\n// PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n// If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n// activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n// - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\n// - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\nvar PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\"\n\n// PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\ntype PodsToActivate struct {\n\tsync.Mutex\n\t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\n\tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\n}\n\n// Clone just returns the same state.\nfunc (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\nfunc NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\n\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\n}\n\n// Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n// message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n// When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n// And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n// NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\ntype Status struct {\n\tcode    Code\n\treasons []string\n\terr     error\n\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n\tplugin string\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n\ts.err = err\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Code returns code of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Code() Code {\n\tif s == nil {\n\t\treturn Success\n\t}\n\treturn s.code\n}\n\n// Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Message() string {\n\tif s == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n}\n\n// SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\nfunc (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n\ts.plugin = plugin\n}\n\n// WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n// and returns the given status object.\nfunc (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\nfunc (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n\treturn s.plugin\n}\n\n// Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n\tif s.err != nil {\n\t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n\t}\n\treturn s.reasons\n}\n\n// AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n}\n\n// IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Success\n}\n\n// IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Wait\n}\n\n// IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Skip\n}\n\n// IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\nfunc (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n\tcode := s.Code()\n\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n}\n\n// AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n// with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) AsError() error {\n\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tif s.err != nil {\n\t\treturn s.err\n\t}\n\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n}\n\n// Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n// cmp.Equal.\nfunc (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n\tif s == nil || x == nil {\n\t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n\t}\n\tif s.code != x.code {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) String() string {\n\treturn s.Message()\n}\n\n// NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\nfunc NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n\ts := &Status{\n\t\tcode:    code,\n\t\treasons: reasons,\n\t}\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\nfunc AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn &Status{\n\t\tcode: Error,\n\t\terr:  err,\n\t}\n}\n\n// WaitingPod represents a pod currently waiting in the permit phase.\ntype WaitingPod interface {\n\t// GetPod returns a reference to the waiting pod.\n\tGetPod() *v1.Pod\n\t// GetPendingPlugins returns a list of pending Permit plugin's name.\n\tGetPendingPlugins() []string\n\t// Allow declares the waiting pod is allowed to be scheduled by the plugin named as \"pluginName\".\n\t// If this is the last remaining plugin to allow, then a success signal is delivered\n\t// to unblock the pod.\n\tAllow(pluginName string)\n\t// Reject declares the waiting pod unschedulable.\n\tReject(pluginName, msg string)\n}\n\n// Plugin is the parent type for all the scheduling framework plugins.\ntype Plugin interface {\n\tName() string\n}\n\n// PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n// Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n// involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n// Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\ntype PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n\tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n}\n\n// LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\ntype LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n\n// QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n// These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n// plugin may be enabled at a time.\ntype QueueSortPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n}\n\n// EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n// move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n// In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n// and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n// Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n// and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n// This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n// and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n//\n// Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n// otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n// And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\ntype EnqueueExtensions interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\n\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\n\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\n\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\n\t//\n\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\n}\n\n// PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n// callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n// state.\ntype PreFilterExtensions interface {\n\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\ntype PreFilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n\t//\n\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n\t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n\t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n\t// Filter again on a specific node.\n\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n}\n\n// FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n// filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n// This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n// These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n// However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n// Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n// running the pod.\ntype FilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n\t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n\t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n\t//\n\t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n\t//\n\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n// after a pod cannot be scheduled.\ntype PostFilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n\t//\n\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t//\n\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n\t//\n\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n}\n\n// PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n// informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n// that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n// state or to generate logs/metrics.\ntype PreScorePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n\t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n\t// the pod will be rejected\n\t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n\t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n\tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\ntype ScoreExtensions interface {\n\t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n\t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n\t// a success status.\n\tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n}\n\n// ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n// nodes that passed the filtering phase.\ntype ScorePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Score is called on each filtered node. Anything other than Success will lead to\n// rejection of the pod.\ntype ReservePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n\t// updated. - There is no guarantee that the information remains unchanged in the binding phase of scheduling.\n\t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in the binding cycle (pre-bind/bind/post-bind/un-reserve info for scheduler framework to act upon PreFilter phase.\ntype PreFilterResult struct {\n\t// The set of nodes that should be considered downstream; if nil then\n\t// all nodes are eligible.\n\tNodeNames sets.Set[string]\n}\n\nfunc (p *PreFilterResult) AllNodes() bool {\n\treturn p == nil || p.NodeNames == nil\n}\n\nfunc (p *PreFilterResult) Merge(in *PreFilterResult) *PreFilterResult {\n\tif p.AllNodes() && in.AllNodes() {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tr := PreFilterResult{}\n\tif p.AllNodes() {\n\t\tr.NodeNames = in.NodeNames.Clone()\n\t\treturn &r\n\t}\n\tif in.AllNodes() {\n\t\tr.NodeNames = p.NodeNames.Clone()\n\t\treturn &r\n\t}\n\n\tr.NodeNames = p.NodeNames.Intersection(in.NodeNames)\n\treturn &r\n}\n\ntype NominatingMode int\n\nconst (\n\tModeNoop NominatingMode = iota\n\tModeOverride\n)\n\ntype NominatingInfo struct {\n\tNominatedNodeName string\n\tNominatingMode    NominatingMode\n}\n\n// PostFilterResult wraps needed info for scheduler &PostFilterResult{\n\t\tNominatingInfo: &NominatingInfo{\n\t\t\tNominatedNodeName: name,\n\t\t\tNominatingMode:    ModeOverride,\n\t\t},\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (ni *NominatingInfo) Mode() NominatingMode {\n\tif ni == nil {\n\t\treturn ModeNoop\n\t}\n\treturn ni.NominatingMode\n}\n\n// PodActivator abstracts operations in the scheduling queue.\ntype PodActivator interface {\n\t// Activate moves the given pods to activeQ.\n\t// If a pod isn't found in unschedulablePods or backoffQ and it's in-flight,\n\t// the wildcard event is registered so that the pod will be requeued when it comes back.\n\t// The core interface definitions for all nine extension points (PreFilter, Filter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, and PostBind) are located in pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go. These interfaces define the contracts that scheduler plugins must implement at each extension point:\\n\\n1. **PreFilterPlugin** (line 512): Called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle, allows plugins to reject pods early or filter nodes.\\n\\n2. **FilterPlugin** (line 540): Filters out nodes that cannot run a pod. This is the core filtering phase where nodes are eliminated.\\n\\n3. **PostFilterPlugin** (line 561): Called after filtering fails, typically used for preemption or other recovery mechanisms.\\n\\n4. **PreScorePlugin** (line 587): Informational extension point called after filtering, allows plugins to record state before scoring.\\n\\n5. **ScorePlugin** (line 607): Scores filtered nodes to determine the best node for pod placement.\\n\\n6. **ReservePlugin** (line 624): Called to reserve resources for a pod before binding. Includes an Unreserve method for rollback.\\n\\n7. **PreBindPlugin** (line 640): Called before pod binding, allows plugins to perform final validations or setup.\\n\\n8. **BindPlugin** (line 673): Responsible for actually binding the pod to a node.\\n\\n9. **PostBindPlugin** (line 649): Called after successful binding, typically used for cleanup or informational purposes.\\n\\n**Framework Implementation and Management:**\\n\\nThe framework implementation that manages these plugins is in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go. The frameworkImpl struct (starting at line 52) stores slices of each plugin type and implements the Framework interface. The getExtensionPoints method (line 103) maps the plugin configuration to the framework's internal plugin slices, providing a centralized mechanism for managing all extension points.\\n\\n**Plugin Registration System:**\\n\\nThe plugin registration system consists of two key components:\\n\\n1. **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go**: Defines the Registry type (line 71), a map from plugin names to PluginFactory functions (line 31). These interfaces define the contracts that scheduler plugins must implement at each extension point:\\n\\n1. **PreFilterPlugin** (line 512): Called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle, allows plugins to reject pods early or filter nodes.\\n\\n2. **FilterPlugin** (line 540): Filters out nodes that cannot run a pod.
